  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_52f3dcd5-c686-431e-a8e1-f43db99171c4'
      });
    }

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/180614-nirkatze">Nirkatze</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The first three books in the series take place before The Emperor of Nihon-ja, due to the fact that the ship Wolfwill is outfitted with the new sail d<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The first three books in the series take place before The Emperor of Nihon-ja, due to the fact that the ship Wolfwill is outfitted with the new sail design. The design was not in use when they last saw Wolfwill's skirl &amp; crew, so the events are probably between Halt's Peril and The Emperor of Nihon-ja. Will is probably about 10 years older than Hal.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_421734386" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421734386" />
    <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington"><img alt="Jonathan Terrington" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478230200p2/6313408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421734386?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Terrington" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington">Jonathan Terrington</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781742750620" href="/book/show/16115601-the-hunters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=favourite-series">favourite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=australian">australian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=new-ya-books-challenge">new-ya-books-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421734386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13764302535100398177"><br/><i>The Hunters</i> is a typical John Flanagan adventure: mature children's fiction with a light-hearted nature, interesting characters, well handled plots, educational information and most of all a rollicking good time. Those familiar with The Rangers Apprentice series may know that Flanagan wrote this series (so far a trilogy) as a spin-off set in the world of Will, Horace and Halt. And yet, despite being a spin-off title, it is no less appealing. <br/><br/><i>The Hunters</i> is the conclusion to the tale of the young</span>
  <span id="freeText13764302535100398177" style="display:none"><br /><i>The Hunters</i> is a typical John Flanagan adventure: mature children's fiction with a light-hearted nature, interesting characters, well handled plots, educational information and most of all a rollicking good time. Those familiar with The Rangers Apprentice series may know that Flanagan wrote this series (so far a trilogy) as a spin-off set in the world of Will, Horace and Halt. And yet, despite being a spin-off title, it is no less appealing. <br /><br /><i>The Hunters</i> is the conclusion to the tale of the young band of vikingesque Skandian warriors led by Hal who set out in book one, The Outcasts, to rescue a Skandian treasure. One of the excellent things about this series, like Rangers Apprentice, is the ability John Flanagan has to create honest character development. He may not be a skilled aesthetic writer but he has a great skill (like Michael Sullivan in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_2_" title="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1-2) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Theft of Swords</a>) of being able to create a taut plot with likeable characters. In other words he has incredible storytelling power and it is this power that makes these novels readable for both the young and the old.<br /><br />As a conclusion to a plot arc <i>The Hunters</i> was both satisfying and intriguing. Though some plot twists could be identified - and being a juvenile targeted novel there were moments of melodramatic silliness - it was on the whole a well executed novel. A novel that leaves the reader desiring more in the series, if only to see the characters develop further. It also is a novel that leaves one wishing that more storytellers could learn to develop characters in such a fashion, in a way that is not forcefully built around a love triangle or what the reader or author wants, but in a way that suits the story. That is what narrative writing is essentially about - not flashy gimmicks, not beautiful prose, but honesty in a way that is beautiful in its essence. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13764302535100398177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12920840385100670200" style="display:none">This book was AMAZING! This series has become one of my all-time favorite series. The characters are so well written that they win you over immediately, and the plot is so engaging that you don't want to put the book down. This series also keeps its excitement throughout the gap between the second and third book; usually your excitement dies down, but it stayed all the way. I also loved that characters from the Ranger Apprentice series are included, because they were loved then and are well appreciated again now. It makes you wonder how much forethought goes into the series because things said a lot earlier are very significant later on. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ In the Rangers Apprentice books, it talks about the triangular shape of the sail, and how the kid who invented it was half-Araluen, and half-Skandian. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Though it isn't that really a spoiler, it just emphasizes the intricate details that are woven into the stories.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1043279212?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1043279212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13371466335697477850">If you know me, you may know I'm a big fan of the Ranger's Apprentice series.<br/><br/>Even still, when I first heard about this series I had mixed feelings. I liked the Skandians well enough in the RA universe, but I wasn't sure about a whole story/series from that angle. And then, after reading the first two books, they didn't quite compare to my beloved RA.<br/><br/>Well, this book changes that.<br/><br/>I'm not saying it surpasses my love, because it's still not quite the same... but I will say that the ending of this bo</span>
  <span id="freeText13371466335697477850" style="display:none">If you know me, you may know I'm a big fan of the Ranger's Apprentice series.<br /><br />Even still, when I first heard about this series I had mixed feelings. I liked the Skandians well enough in the RA universe, but I wasn't sure about a whole story/series from that angle. And then, after reading the first two books, they didn't quite compare to my beloved RA.<br /><br />Well, this book changes that.<br /><br />I'm not saying it surpasses my love, because it's still not quite the same... but I will say that the ending of this book was pretty damn awesome. It completes the arc that started in the first book - Flanagan seems rather fond of these multi-book arcs. I figure it goes back to his TV heritage - and it does it in an exciting and suspensful finale.<br /><br />The characters continue to develop and come to life - with the exception of Stefan, who felt mostly shunted to the side for most of this book. Hal, Thorn, Ingvar and Lydia stand out as exceptional characters, and even the twins are growing on me (though they kind remind me a bit much of the twins in How to Train Your Dragon).<br /><br />With this book, even though it completes the arc, the series has gone from "when I get around to it" to "really looking forward to the next". I'm really glad, too, because I was a bit worried about the upcoming crossover with characters from both the RA and Brotherband series - but now I'm really excited for it. :&gt;<br /><br /><br />My only real gripe is that I could do without the love triangle thing. I do appreciate that it's not a main focus, as is often the case with far too many YA books, but, honestly, I could live without it entirely.</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hazel West" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hazel West" href="/user/show/6747285-hazel-west">Hazel West</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6747285-hazel-west?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6747285-hazel-west?shelf=great-summer-reads">great-summer-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6747285-hazel-west?shelf=brothers-in-arms-books">brothers-in-arms-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351613899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17084258689204941889">Thoughts on the Overall Book: Whereas the last book tended to drag a little, I think this was was properly more fast-paced and exciting and I'm glad it ended the way it did. I really enjoyed it a lot. It had all the great character moments, adventure and humor that I have come to expect in John Flanagan's books. I've come to like the Brotherband Chronicles just as much as the Ranger's Apprentice series.<br/><br/>Characters: As always, I loved the Heron Brotherband, plus Thorn. They are totally awesome. I'</span>
  <span id="freeText17084258689204941889" style="display:none">Thoughts on the Overall Book: Whereas the last book tended to drag a little, I think this was was properly more fast-paced and exciting and I'm glad it ended the way it did. I really enjoyed it a lot. It had all the great character moments, adventure and humor that I have come to expect in John Flanagan's books. I've come to like the Brotherband Chronicles just as much as the Ranger's Apprentice series.<br /><br />Characters: As always, I loved the Heron Brotherband, plus Thorn. They are totally awesome. I'm also glad we kind of had more of a chance to get to know some of the other boys in this one too like Ingvar and Edvin, both of whom I have come to like quite a bit. Lydia, I still kind of feel was just thrown into the story to have a female character. She had her moments, but there was only one instance where she really did anything that the others couldn't have done, and even then, it still could have been accomplished just with the boys. I just can't seem to get to know her or care for her as much as I did for Alyss in the Ranger's Apprentice series. I know John Flanagan can write good female characters, but Lydia just kind of falls flat for me. I am totally glad there was no stupid love triangle between her, Hal and Stig though which was what I was really afraid would happen in this book. In fact, I'm kind of rooting for her and Ingvar ;) As for the villains, I still love Zavak, again, he's a great pirate character. I also liked Doutro because he was interesting and really nasty, though I kind of wish there had been more of him and that he had played more into the plot. <br /><br />Writing Style: As always, I love John Flanagan's writing style. This book was no different than any of the others.<br /><br />Problems/What bothered me: Nothing really bothered me, except I still think Lydia wasn't nessessary, and then there was that one part at the place with Doutro that almost seemed like a lose end, but it's easily overlooked and doesn't take away from the story.<br /><br />Conclusion: 4 Stars. Really liked this installment, and I'm totally excited to see what will happen next. Apart from the duel, I think the epilogue was my favorite part of the book. It was so perfect in so many ways =)<br /><br />Recommended Audience: Long time John Flanagan fans, of course. And if you haven't read Brotherband yet, do so! They're just as good as Ranger's Apprentice!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17084258689204941889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_456149580" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/456149580" />
    <a title="Gail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4362439-gail"><img alt="Gail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286402432p2/4362439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/456149580?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gail" href="/user/show/4362439-gail">Gail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer456149580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14908529995082819907">At first, I felt like this book was a little too contrived. Don't get me wrong, I really like the Ranger's Apprentice series and how Mr. Flanagan spins his stories so that they have good moral lessons, but the beginning of this one (Brotherband series) was well---too forced. I liked the story. I like the characters. At the middle of the book, the story picked up a little and I loved the ending. I could really visualize the two ships fighting and how people would be impressed by the youthful grou</span>
  <span id="freeText14908529995082819907" style="display:none">At first, I felt like this book was a little too contrived. Don't get me wrong, I really like the Ranger's Apprentice series and how Mr. Flanagan spins his stories so that they have good moral lessons, but the beginning of this one (Brotherband series) was well---too forced. I liked the story. I like the characters. At the middle of the book, the story picked up a little and I loved the ending. I could really visualize the two ships fighting and how people would be impressed by the youthful group and their abilities. I especially like how the author includes competent,strong, girls in his books. Flanagan's Ranger's Apprentice books are better than the Brotherband books. They teach many good lessons of loyalty, determination, friendship and they aren't as forced as these books are, but still these are good reads and good lesson builders for boys. In this series, we read about Thorn, who feels less of a person since he lost his hand and how he gains purpose again directing this group of boys--there is a good lesson. We also see how good leadership can bring a group together and work together. The funny part of this book was how one of the crewmen decided to knit and at first they thought less of him and then when they saw his hats, they all wanted one. (Good lesson there too) so if you want your son to read a good rollicking story with moral lessons intertwined within it, these are the books for your son 10-12 years old. They will be hooked.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14908529995082819907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3149050585952389426">This book jumped right in where book two left off. Now I must say one thing I love about John’s writing is that he makes his fight scenes accurate, but not gory. He can describe a tortured man yet keep me interested and not disgusted. Like I can visualize it being gross but it isn’t gory. I know I repeated myself but I don’t know the best way to word that. Can’t wait for the next book!<br/><br/>Happy Reading 📖 </span>

<div id="review_659039471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/659039471" />
    <a title="Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13641528-sue"><img alt="Sue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385611661p2/13641528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/659039471?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue" href="/user/show/13641528-sue">Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781742750620" href="/book/show/16115601-the-hunters">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer659039471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11494275203435926011">The third instalment in the Brotherband Chronicles is, I think the best. Fast-paced, great plot movement and battle scenes (particularly the epic battle between the Heron and Zavac's pirate ship, Raven near the end) are brilliant. I could really picture the action in my head and at one point it got so exciting I could not turn the pages fast enough!<br/>Hal and his crew, including Thorn and the newest member, Lydia, are in hot pursuit of the Raven and Zavac's, whose band of pirates stole the Andomal </span>
  <span id="freeText11494275203435926011" style="display:none">The third instalment in the Brotherband Chronicles is, I think the best. Fast-paced, great plot movement and battle scenes (particularly the epic battle between the Heron and Zavac's pirate ship, Raven near the end) are brilliant. I could really picture the action in my head and at one point it got so exciting I could not turn the pages fast enough!<br />Hal and his crew, including Thorn and the newest member, Lydia, are in hot pursuit of the Raven and Zavac's, whose band of pirates stole the Andomal (an important Skandian relic) form their village. Lydia is out for Zavac's blood because of the death and destruction he brought to her village, Limmat. This story really sees us getting to know the characters and their quirks much better. There is suspense, drama, comedy and emotion throughout, and all done with aplomb. Many reviewers seem to thinks this is the last in the series, but I am pretty sure there will be more and the final pages certainly leave room for it. I will be very surprised if it stops at number 3!<br />In any case, this is a great read and I recommend it for anyone from 8 to 80. Flanagan's humour and eye for details is evident in spades and will win over the most reluctant reader. I look forward to many more adventures with the Heron and her crew - and if it is not to be, I will just re-read the three I have!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11494275203435926011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_433692022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/433692022" />
    <a title="Joyce Zarins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10425409-joyce-zarins"><img alt="Joyce Zarins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449686391p2/10425409.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/433692022?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joyce Zarins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joyce Zarins" href="/user/show/10425409-joyce-zarins">Joyce Zarins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer433692022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6248183885342558290">The Hunters opens as the Heron has crossed the Stormwhite Sea heading for Raguza, a pirate stronghold on the Schuyt River. On board are the eight original members of the Brotherband including one who was injured during the battle, and also Lydia the Limmatan hunter, Thorn the Seawolf, and a captured Magyaran pirate. <br/>Lydia has made a commitment as the only female involved in the hazardous venture ahead. She proved her effectiveness at killing pirates in the Limmatan battle and will follow that no</span>
  <span id="freeText6248183885342558290" style="display:none">The Hunters opens as the Heron has crossed the Stormwhite Sea heading for Raguza, a pirate stronghold on the Schuyt River. On board are the eight original members of the Brotherband including one who was injured during the battle, and also Lydia the Limmatan hunter, Thorn the Seawolf, and a captured Magyaran pirate. <br />Lydia has made a commitment as the only female involved in the hazardous venture ahead. She proved her effectiveness at killing pirates in the Limmatan battle and will follow that now with additional strategic skills she alone in this group has. Thorn comes to admire her abilities, expanding his own parameters and the boys accept her, in spite of some reservations about having a team member who is female. She has an active role in the harrowing conflicts that ensue and is gradually recognized as a full member of the crew, signified by her being given the new Brotherband insignia to wear. Her problem solving skills and fighting abilities are on a par with that of the boys. Her presence injects moments of light romantic competition, although these are appropriately not major factors in the story. <br />One of the boys takes up a craft normally thought of as women’s work during the era of the story’s setting and initially receives ridicule for it until it proves to be of practical value and eventually becomes symbolic of unity. As with The Outcasts and The Invaders, in The Hunters the tense conflict-laden moments in the story are offset by interjected humor. Characters banter, sparring hilariously with non sequiturs, withering looks, puns and sarcasm. They sound like a real bunch of guys (and gal). <br />Pivotal parts of The Hunters seriously challenge Hal’s abilities and decision-making skills as the Brotherband get themselves deep into the pirates’ treacherous snakepit. Each time he is faced with potentially deadly choices, Hal is sleepless while turning every option over in his mind to be sure the strategy he takes is the most propitious. One of these involves a natural obstacle that requires supreme effort and cooperation from everyone on board for them to survive. Another requires psychological strategy and insight into the minds of devious people. Hal takes risks, always including everyone else in the group to achieve consensus, elicit additional ideas, and factor out problems he has not foreseen. He is a wise and fair leader of this deadly group of pirate hunters. Hal and crew work on their skills and strategies constantly to improve their chances. However, like the River Dan, this plot has many surprising twists and turns.<br />By page 315 this reader was convinced that Zavak had taken the all-important goal of the Brotherband’s pursuit from where Hal thought it was to secrete it somewhere new, and that Zavac in the Raven would escape yet again, that elusive snake. At that moment the local Korpaljo made a declaration that will make the Brotherband’s goals impossible to achieve – even for them. So Hal surprises everyone by suggesting what seems like a truly foolhardy move. Everyone is suitably shocked and his own crew doubt this decision. He adds a caveat that slightly narrows the odds, but it will be a fight to the death and most bets are with the Magyarans.<br />Since the Brotherband Chronicles is about teens who have trained to be warriors, the violence aspect is embedded. In The Outcasts it is mild – they are still in training – and this part of the story could be for kids 10 and up. Once the Brotherband members have graduated and head out on their risky mission, the violence becomes more overt. There are accounts of the murderous behavior of Zavak and his men in torturing the doomed captive ship captain, even going beyond the pain they need to inflict to get the information they want. During the battle in Limmat many pirates are killed by Heron crew members and their allies using swords, arrows, fire, and other weapons. One of the Heron crew is wounded with an arrow and nearly dies. The purpose of the fighting at Limmat is to save the townspeople from the pirates, so the violence is not gratuitous, but perhaps the readership of this volume should be 12 and up. Then in The Hunters, Hal and his crew are actively going after the pirates in order to retrieve the object of their quest and thereby clear their names back in Hallsholm. Lydia’s purpose is revenge. These are not defensive or altruistic motives and the actions of Hal and his crew result in many deaths, some of which are hand-to-hand. Although the pirates have been a deadly scourge and needed to be dealt with, they are still humans. There is no savoring of blood and gore on the part of the Brotherband, but there is also no mercy, making this more appropriate for older kids – perhaps 14 and up. Parents should decide.<br />Is this story educational? The sailing and ship handling certainly make seafaring skills more understandable and exciting and the author has provided a glossary of nautical terms at the beginning, a good take-away. The changing relationships and growing social strategies between the characters will give young readers good insights into personal dynamics. Advanced vocabulary throughout – diffidently, supercilious, placatory, denouement, e.g. - is paired with humor, faux expletives like “Orlog’s toenails!” along with contemporary expressions like “slow on the uptake”.<br />Is it fun to read? Oh, yes. The Brotherband Chronicles series is compelling, dramatic, entertaining and suspenseful. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6248183885342558290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_484505185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484505185" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/484505185?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer484505185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15984245205595175026">Third in the Brotherband Chronicles urban fantasy series for young adults. It is an offshoot from Flanagan's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=✓&query=John+Flanagan%2C+ranger+apprentice' title='Lists all the books in Flanagan's Ranger Apprentice series in Goodreads' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ranger Apprentice</a> series.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>This was great! Again. I haven't yet read a bad book from John Flanagan. And it keeps amazing me that we're only three books into the series. I feel as though I know the characters so well and been on so many adventures with them, that there must be more than just three books!??<br/><br/>I do love how Flanagan creates such a positive role model with the crew of the <em>H</em></span>
  <span id="freeText15984245205595175026" style="display:none">Third in the Brotherband Chronicles urban fantasy series for young adults. It is an offshoot from Flanagan's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=✓&amp;query=John+Flanagan%2C+ranger+apprentice" title="Lists all the books in Flanagan's Ranger Apprentice series in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Ranger Apprentice</a> series.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />This was great! Again. I haven't yet read a bad book from John Flanagan. And it keeps amazing me that we're only three books into the series. I feel as though I know the characters so well and been on so many adventures with them, that there must be more than just three books!??<br /><br />I do love how Flanagan creates such a positive role model with the crew of the <em>Heron</em> and how inventive they all are. I particularly enjoyed the shock various adults received when they realized that Hal was the actual captain of the <em>Heron</em>!<br /><br /><blockquote>"Must admit, I had a few sleepless moments."<br /><br />Thorn raised an eyebrow. "Only a few?"<br /><br />"Two, actually. One lasted for the first two days. The other for the next two."</blockquote><br /><br />Oh, the knitting! I love it. From ridicule to begging as the boys discover the benefits of Edvin's labors. I do feel a degree of skepticism about the effects of the willow bark, but I also appreciate the idea behind Flanagan including it. A nice bit of medicinal lore. Hee-hee-hee, Zavac has hoist himself with his own petard! I love it. Oh, then there's the duel. Oh, yeah!<br /><br />It takes teamwork and trust for the boys to get as far as they do; a bond they began building at the beginning in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10551947-the-outcasts" title="Opens John Flanagan's Outcasts in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Outcasts</em>
</a>.<br /><br />It's adventure without horror and lots of laughter to be had at the expense of the opposition.<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />With Rikard's help, the <em>Heron</em> follows the <em>Raven</em> to the Dan River. Unfortunately for them, Zavac has left a man behind to pick up an order of rope. And Vargas thinks quickly and acts even quicker, setting all sorts of traps for the boys.<br /><br />A corrupt mayor who jails them and thinks to steal their ship while planning to enslave Lydia. A whitewater raceway no ship can sail. A pirate haven they cannot enter.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><strong>Hal</strong> leads this merry band of teens as their skirl. The rest of the runaway crew includes <strong>Stig</strong>, who is Hal's second-in-command; <strong>Stefan</strong>; <strong>Edvin</strong> is their medic and crew cook (Hal intends to train him in steering); <strong>Jesper</strong> is skilled at thieving and sneaking about; <strong>Ingvar</strong> is terribly nearsighted and was badly wounded; and, <strong>Ulf</strong> and <strong>Wulf</strong> are the argumentative twins who excel at handling the sails. <strong>Lydia Demarek</strong> is the girl they took on board after the battle in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13003565-the-invaders" title="Opens John Flanagan's Invaders in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Invaders</em>
</a>. She's quite skilled with her chosen weapons and tracking ability...as Thorn is forced to admit! Old <strong>Thorn</strong> may be crippled without a hand, but he has more than made up for it. His knowledge and skills don't require a hand. Besides, Hal's inventive skills creates all sorts of specialized tools. <br /><br /><strong>Erak</strong> is Oberjarl of the Skandians; <strong>Svengal</strong> is his old friend; and, <strong>Karina</strong> is Hal's mother. <strong>Tursgud</strong> is the former leader of the Sharks brotherband.<br /><br /><strong>Rickard</strong> is the Magyaran pirate Thorn captured in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13003565-the-invaders" title="Opens John Flanagan's Invaders in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Invaders</em>
</a>. <strong>Vargas</strong> is one of Zacar's men, who stayed behind to pick up an order of rope. He hasn't any conscience and is quite tricky. <strong>Zacar</strong> is the captain of the <em>Raven</em>, and the thief who stole the Andomal that the boys were supposed to be guarding. It's a matter of honor now. The boys have to retrieve it if they ever want to go home.<br /><br />The <strong>Gatmeister</strong> is the mayor of Bayrath and <strong>Doutro</strong> is quite willing to do anything if he's paid enough. <strong>Pedr</strong> is a fellow inmate, jailed for winning from Doutro. <strong>Dana</strong> is Doutro's cook; <strong>Milo</strong> is the senior servant; <strong>Erlic</strong> is the idiot they set to guard Lydia. <strong>Mihaly</strong> is the Korpaljo of the the pirate haven of Raguza. A former pirate himself, he knows all their tricks and doesn't tolerate betrayal.<br /><br /><strong>Mannoc</strong> is the skipper of the <em>Seahawk</em>, which is guarding a trader convoy. <strong>Algon</strong>, <strong>Freyth</strong>, and <strong>Crenna</strong> are the trader captains.<br /><br /><b>The Cover</b><br />The cover is awash in a churning sea as, I'm assuming, Hal braces himself on the deck of his ship with one knee raised while taking aim with a crossbow. It's all blue-green seas, the brown of the ship and the wooden arch overhead as well as the brown leathers in which Hal is wrapped. Except for the watch cap on his head, Edvin's work. I'd've been more impressed if the cover artist had Hal getting ready to shoot the Mangler, though.<br /><br />The title is what this series has been about so far: <em>The Hunters</em> tracking down Zavac and his <em>Raven</em>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15984245205595175026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_427221142" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/427221142" />
    <a title="Mara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6879652-mara"><img alt="Mara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380254226p2/6879652.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/427221142?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mara" href="/user/show/6879652-mara">Mara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6879652-mara?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6879652-mara?shelf=kingdom-adventure">kingdom-adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer427221142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2580998462049800544"><b>Cover Blurb:</b> Yes or No? Yes. Despite the fact that there is a “character impersonator” on the front, his face is not defined all that much, so I’m okay with it. I do love the cover art for this series; it’s exciting, and I love how each picture refers to some specific part in the corresponding book.<br/><br/><b>Characters:</b> All of the Herons remain really good characters. Hal is a great protagonist, Stig a wonderful “second,” Ulf and Wulf and all the others great in all their roles. Thorn is a character who c</span>
  <span id="freeText2580998462049800544" style="display:none"><b>Cover Blurb:</b> Yes or No? Yes. Despite the fact that there is a “character impersonator” on the front, his face is not defined all that much, so I’m okay with it. I do love the cover art for this series; it’s exciting, and I love how each picture refers to some specific part in the corresponding book.<br /><br /><b>Characters:</b> All of the Herons remain really good characters. Hal is a great protagonist, Stig a wonderful “second,” Ulf and Wulf and all the others great in all their roles. Thorn is a character who continually grows on me. My initial impression of him at the beginning of the series was a sad Halt wanna-be. But something about him really clicked with me in this latest installment, and I no longer think of him as a Halt substitute. Zavac continued to be a really good villain for this series; he was a believable pirate, ruthless, cunning. While still not my absolute favorite villain out of <i>all</i> of Flanagan’s books, he fit this particular story. Now for Lydia, the girl character. I’ll admit, she proves her usefulness in this one, but there is absolutely no reason why she couldn’t have been a twelve-year-old boy. She doesn’t have The Attitude, but she didn’t seem to be able to take a joke and her continual sassing of Thorn got on my nerves. I’m okay with characters who show their friendly affection through sarcastic banter, but when Lydia said something, it felt more disrespectful than affectionate, and it did bring her perilously close to having an Attitude.<br /><br /><b>The Romance:</b> The potential love triangle between Hal, Lydia, and Stig does not get much of an opportunity to surface in this installment, for which I am eternally grateful. But it’s hovering there in the background, threatening to ruin future books. I don’t want to see Stig and Hal be at odds with each other over a girl, least of all Lydia, who honestly doesn’t seem worth it.<br /><br /><b>Plot:</b> This is what makes me say that out of the three books so far, this is the best one. The other two books spent a lot of time on the Herons training themselves, and while it allowed the Reader to see their camaraderie strengthen into an unbreakable bond, it also got boring after a while. For a brief second, <i>The Hunters</i> threatened to sink into yet more brotherband training, but the Author thankfully only devotes not even a whole chapter to it, and that’s the last we hear of it. The rest of the book is spent with the Herons actually hunting Zavac down, running into obstacles, and outsmarting Zavac’s allies. It was exciting! There’s a jail break and sneaking away in the dead of night; false murder accusations and disguises, and as a grand finale, a duel. The Herons’ ruse for getting into Raguza was genuinely clever; I really enjoyed it.<br /><br /><b>Believability:</b> Flanagan has always been good at presenting Readers with battle strategies and plans that are plausible, and he has always written realistic battles, with realistic wounds. Lydia realistically doesn’t engage any pirates in a hand-to-hand fight, but relies on a long-range weapon, since she doesn’t have the strength to hold her own in a close-quarters fight. The one thing that struck me as incorrect was the rapidity which willow bark tea clears up one of the character’s fever. Willowbark works well, but considering how bad of a temperature the boy has, it wouldn’t clear the fever <i>completely</i> up in less than an hour.<br /><br /><b>Writing Style:</b> At times, the Author tries a little too hard to be funny, like with the knitting scene and the Heron ballad at the end. I found those two scenes to just be silly. He also uses a dialogue ploy which I absolutely hate. I <i>really</i> don’t like bits of dialogue where a character asks a question that the Reader just might be wondering, for the sole purpose of having another character provide the answer. It’s a very choppy method of putting the Reader’s questions to rest, and often disrupts the story’s flow. Apart from that, Flanagan’s writing is as it has always been: entertaining. He shows his prowess at writing sea battles in this book, which is amazingly good. <br /><br /><b>Content:</b> None.<br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b> The end was exciting, fast-paced, and not dragged out. It got to the point. I’m usually not okay with the villain and hero having a one-on-one showdown during a big battle because it’s so unlikely, but in this case I was fine with it, because a ship is significantly smaller than a battlefield, so if someone is actively seeking out another, it’s plausible. As a whole, I really liked <i>The Hunters.</i> It was definitely the best out of the three.<br /><br /><b>Recommended Audience:</b> John Flanagan fans, even those who gave up on the <i>Ranger’s Apprentice</i> series. Girl-and-guy read, any age.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2580998462049800544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2962557137" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2962557137" />
    <a title="Jared Bird" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13476472-jared-bird"><img alt="Jared Bird" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349703435p2/13476472.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2962557137?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jared Bird" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jared Bird" href="/user/show/13476472-jared-bird">Jared Bird</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2962557137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16296933079574777845">This book is easily the best paced of the three, and probably the most satisfying. My biggest issue with the previous book was how it didn’t seem to get much accomplished for the overarching plot, but it did set up for some very interesting scenes in this book. The book has three major parts to it, each taking place in a different city, and as the boys worked their way from city to city, I kept thinking to myself “these stories are so unique”. The plots that twist throughout this book are so muc</span>
  <span id="freeText16296933079574777845" style="display:none">This book is easily the best paced of the three, and probably the most satisfying. My biggest issue with the previous book was how it didn’t seem to get much accomplished for the overarching plot, but it did set up for some very interesting scenes in this book. The book has three major parts to it, each taking place in a different city, and as the boys worked their way from city to city, I kept thinking to myself “these stories are so unique”. The plots that twist throughout this book are so much more interesting than what you would normally find in a young adult novel. Each city was more interesting than the last.<br /><br />This book closes out the story spanning the previous two books and I’m excited to see where it goes next. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16296933079574777845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1157194347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1157194347" />
    <a title="Diana Nazarchuk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18810512-diana-nazarchuk"><img alt="Diana Nazarchuk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420491827p2/18810512.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1157194347?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana Nazarchuk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana Nazarchuk" href="/user/show/18810512-diana-nazarchuk">Diana Nazarchuk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1157194347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3669319700579066820">John Flanagan has one again impressed me with the amazingly written third book in the Brotherband Chronicles adventure series: The Hunters. Hal and the Heron crew, take you on an unforgettable experience full with dangerous fighting and flying across the blue ocean waters in their unique ship in pursuit of the man who took everything away from them and the Scandinavian nation. The malefic pirate Zavac. <br/>	The Herons spend most of their time sailing the vast ocean trying in search of the Andomal: t</span>
  <span id="freeText3669319700579066820" style="display:none">John Flanagan has one again impressed me with the amazingly written third book in the Brotherband Chronicles adventure series: The Hunters. Hal and the Heron crew, take you on an unforgettable experience full with dangerous fighting and flying across the blue ocean waters in their unique ship in pursuit of the man who took everything away from them and the Scandinavian nation. The malefic pirate Zavac. <br />	The Herons spend most of their time sailing the vast ocean trying in search of the Andomal: their treasure. I especially like that Hal, the skirl, or captain, is so young, yet when it comes to being a leader, or making important decisions, Hal always makes the right one, acting like a mature adult. However, he cannot do so without his loyal best friend Stig, who is always ready to stand up for Hal, and any of the crewmembers. Along their journey they pickup Lydia, who will become a Heron when she shows her abilities in their search and their fights. Then there is Thorn. One can call him misleading, yet he is what keeps the Herons together. He acts as if he does not care much about anything, but he gives advice to the young crew boys who are only just beginning their life at sea. The Herons are afraid of him and underestimate his capabilities but they know that he has spent his life at sea and that he knows what he’s talking about. Together, Hal, Stig, Thorn, Stephan, Ulf and Wulf (the twins), Jesper, Edvin and Ingvar, are the Herons.<br />	 They sail from town to town looking for Zavac and his crew over various terrains that he has never seen before. I like the mystery behind it, because you do not know if they are going to find and fight him or if he will escape from them. Enemies come up with plans to try to shut away the brotherband and many attempts are made on the crews’ life. I like that the author portrays that teamwork is very important to overcome obstacles, the Herons definitely know that, and it makes them closer as friends. One of my favorite parts of the book was when the Herons were preparing to fight and Thorn shows how proud he is to be part of the amazing Heron crew. It also shows another side of Thorn and how much he really cares about them. <br />“’See this helmet?’ <br />Thorns booming question took him by surprise. The old sea wolf had moved away from the keel box to a position in the very center of the ship. He was pointing to the massive horned helmet he wore-the treasured headgear of all Skandian warriors.<br />‘I’ve had this helmet for nigh on thirty years. I’ve worn it on raids. I’ve worn it in battles. It’s seen more action in its time than most warriors you’ll ever meet. It’s saved my lie on a dozen occasions. And I’ve been proud to wear it. It’s the symbol of a Skandian warrior.’ <br />He had the attention of everyone on board now. Then he stepped to the port rail and removed the helmet. <br />‘But I don’t want it anymore.’<br />The was an audible intake of breath from the entire crew as he drew back his left arm and tossed the helmet high into the air, so that it arched, then tumbled, sinning slowly, end over end, into the sea. All eyes followed its trajectory and someone let out a cry of amazement as the helmet threw up a white splash, surprisingly smaller than they expected, then disappeared. When they looked back to Thorn, he was wearing new piece of headgear. He had pulled on his black watch cap, with the white outline of a heron on it. <br />‘This is the symbol I choose to wear now. The Heron borotherband symbol. Ne beat-up helmet could make me as proud as this.’<br />There was a moment of stunned silence. Then the entire crew began cheering as he grinned at them, nodding his head and pointing to the black watch cap, identical to the ones they all wore.” <br />	 This passage, I think, sums up how good the Herons really are, because if Thorn is willing to become part of the Herons, and leave his past behind, then you know that they are really something special. <br />	Overall, I think that this book is beautifully written and will have you on edge, anticipation the next page and chapter. Moreover, you will want to read on in this incredible Brotherband Chronicles series. I know that I definitely do. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3669319700579066820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1363735614" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1363735614" />
    <a title="John Parrish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45968323-john-parrish"><img alt="John Parrish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439639120p2/45968323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1363735614?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Parrish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Parrish" href="/user/show/45968323-john-parrish">John Parrish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1363735614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1043077935244984135">"The Hunters", Written by John Flanigan, is the third book in the Brotherband chronicles. The Brotherband Chronicles being a spin-off series to the famous "Rangers Apprentice" series.<br/><br/>Following the battle of Limmat in the previous book, Hal and his Heron brotherband take on a girl from Limmat,Lydia.As they continue their persuit of the pirate Zavac,the pirate that stole Skandias' prized treasure, the Andomel,on the very night the Heron brotherband were tasked to defend it. A pursuit that,as they </span>
  <span id="freeText1043077935244984135" style="display:none">"The Hunters", Written by John Flanigan, is the third book in the Brotherband chronicles. The Brotherband Chronicles being a spin-off series to the famous "Rangers Apprentice" series.<br /><br />Following the battle of Limmat in the previous book, Hal and his Heron brotherband take on a girl from Limmat,Lydia.As they continue their persuit of the pirate Zavac,the pirate that stole Skandias' prized treasure, the Andomel,on the very night the Heron brotherband were tasked to defend it. A pursuit that,as they discover, will take them to the lawless pirate haven,Raguza. But before they can even continue the chase, Ingvar fell ill and may not survive the rest of the journey....<br /><br />Main characters<br />Hal- A half Araluen half Skandian boy, Skirl(captain) of the ship "The Heron" and leader of the Heron Brotherband<br />Physical traits-Brown fair,Fair skin,average height (about 5"11),Slim<br />Personality traits-inventor(although not always a successful one),natural leader,gifted helmsmen,caring(if only to his crew),intelligent(at least as intelligent as Skandians can be),<br />Stig-Hal first mate, the son of a laundry woman and absentee gambling father who ran away after being unable to pay debts. <br />Physical traits-Shoulder length white hair, fair skin,wide chest, muscular arms,tall (around 6"2)<br />Personality traits-Short temper,quick to violence,expert warrior,antisocial(counting only Hal as a friend).<br />Edvin-more brains than brawn, Edvin is the healer and cook of the Herons crew<br />Physical traits-slim,short blond hair,fair skin,short(about 5"5),weak <br />Personality traits- shy,extremely intelligent,lacking self confidence<br />Jesper-A former thief who people still won't trust<br />Physical traits-strong runner,very slim,<br />Personality traits-stubborn,overconfident,<br />Ulf and Wulf-Two twins who constantly tricking people into thinking one is the other.<br />Physical traits, brown hair,stocky,muscular arms,fair skin<br />Psychological traits-mischievous,quiet<br />Stefan-Lookout in the group<br />Physical traits slim,fair skin,strong legs<br />Psychological traits-joker,loyal,compassionate<br />Lydia-The only girl in the crew, a hunter and tracker from Limmat instead of Skandia <br />Physical traits-long brown hair,olive skin,thin muscular legs,slim<br />Psychological traits-Intelligent,manipulative,cunning,independent,easily irritated<br />Thorn-the oldest in the group, a retired warrior and adviser to Hal <br />physical traits-one handed,shaggy,brown beard,stocky<br />Psychological traits-loyal,open-minded<br />Ingvar-the massive boy who is the only who can target with the mangler,a massive crossbow mounted on the bow of the ship.<br />Physical traits-extremely tall(closer to seven foot than to six),wide chest,muscular arms,visually impaired to the point he cannot fight(in pre-glasses time).<br />Psychological traits-very loyal,trusting,caring,compassionate,aware of his own disability. <br /><br />The plot moved quite slower than in the last two books, it seemed as though far more time was devoted to the characters than to the action. Ingvar was written very well and is personally my favorite character. He always had that "gentile giant" kind of personality where he understood characters and respected them, but would still throw them overboard if Hal asked him to.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to those who like Rangers Apprentice(for obvious reasons) or those who like The Lord of The Rings series because the book has that discovery of a brand new world with brand new places,friends,and enemies. </span>

<div id="review_729405133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/729405133" />
    <a title="Katrina Ly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5044885-katrina-ly"><img alt="Katrina Ly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353925962p2/5044885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/729405133?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katrina Ly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katrina Ly" href="/user/show/5044885-katrina-ly">Katrina Ly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer729405133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9244534697137432767">Before I write anything else, you guys should probably know I actually rated this closer to 4.5 than 5 stars.<br/><br/>MOVING ON, I read this book a few days back and while its obviously a very well written book, with very well developed characters, I still feel as if there is some kind of distance separating me from the characters, or more specifically the main one, and because of that distance I can't bring myself to actually GIVE it a full five stars (in my mind not the site, my mind). So while everyth</span>
  <span id="freeText9244534697137432767" style="display:none">Before I write anything else, you guys should probably know I actually rated this closer to 4.5 than 5 stars.<br /><br />MOVING ON, I read this book a few days back and while its obviously a very well written book, with very well developed characters, I still feel as if there is some kind of distance separating me from the characters, or more specifically the main one, and because of that distance I can't bring myself to actually GIVE it a full five stars (in my mind not the site, my mind). So while everything else, such as a hilarious sense of humour John Flanagan always incorporates into his books, clever, BELIEVABLE (thank god) dialogue and a very interesting plot, were all there i still can't give the book a full 5 stars.<br /><br />Why oh why does Hal have to be so perfect?! I mean (and I'm sorry for doing this- i don't usually make a habit of comparing books with other books but...) compared to Will from Ranger's apprentice, even though his still obviously a very root-able character who anyone can easily fall in love with and read about for the rest of their lives, he just doesn't seem as REAL the way Will was. And that is pretty much the heart of the problem for me right now. Everything else is perfect. Just perfect. But please, I beg you John Flannagan, give him SOMETHING to make him more human because right now he kinda reminds me of those perfect characters you sometimes read about in novels who always manage to make the right decisions and end up becoming, you know, THAT person. The person everyone looks up to and practically worships. It's like his a saint or something.<br /><br />Other than that though, I really did enjoy this story. It had me reading well into the night and into the early morning chirpings of those crazy birds who wake up at the break of dawn :) it's very much a kids novel at the moment but whatever. I'm really looking forward to reading about Hal and his crew and how they'll grow up and face any future challenges that may arise :)<br /><br />Overall, a very very well-written book complete with quite a few sigh-worthy scenes that will just touch you in the heart and make you smile just because. A book very well worth the read :)<br /><br />Cheers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9244534697137432767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14021991130272563675" style="display:none">In the third book in the Brotherband Chronicles, Hal and the crew of the Heron have just missed capturing Zavac the stolen Andomal and set off to follow him once more. Set aside enough time to read this all in one day if you can, because once you dive in , you won't want to stop.</span>

In this finale, the reader follows Hal and the Herons as they reach the end of their long journey in search of the one thing that will clear their names, the one thing that made them pariahs within the Skandian world: the most prized possession of the Skandians, the Andomal.   <span id="freeText7771400756914009105" style="display:none">The Hunters is the final book in the Brotherband Chronicles trilogy written by the author of the Ranger's Apprentice series, John Flanagan. In this finale, the reader follows Hal and the Herons as they reach the end of their long journey in search of the one thing that will clear their names, the one thing that made them pariahs within the Skandian world: the most prized possession of the Skandians, the Andomal. This is a very satisfying conclusion to the trilogy because John Flanagan offers all the usual action that is present in his fantastical series, but he offers more engaging characters and their changes throughout the story. If you've have read the first two books of this series than this one is a must. </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21467217-emma-clement?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1637971444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer676799121014093814">Lots of action, fighting, twists, and turns - this novel was great! A crazy story keeping me glued to the pages so I read it in one sitting! <br/><br/>This book did a great job expanding on the feminist topics it introduced in the last novel-like the fact that a girl can be a great warrior, or a big strong man can enjoy knitting. Well done! Quite a progressive book in that aspect, especially as it is written for kids. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1794712189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1794712189" />
    <a title="Conor Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58877291-conor-bradley"><img alt="Conor Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474982999p2/58877291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1794712189?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Conor Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Conor Bradley" href="/user/show/58877291-conor-bradley">Conor Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1794712189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2372758650542347152">The Hunters is a great book for adventurous and exciting people because this book is full of it. Hal, Thorn, and the Heron brother band sail down the Dan river chasing Zavac the pirate. Along the way they encounter pirates, boastful leaders, and a friendly ship that escorts traders. They must think and barge through all the obstacles Zavac leaves to catch up to him. Sail through the library and pick up the Hunters and read to your victory.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+IoM/32/Kw39WQOnXV61+32OZl9v5aFD7j6iqyGmLv7UwWr3lp1PpOLwf3T6h8oMHXa2hcVMEAbyotLSt+4fNw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('He91njjih5zaWH9GgASfFNRSNu331OVoyMTDHXE3YkoxpBOW08DjNcXxA5Un3eDjtKrmN119VC3UWLNk539Tgw==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText14657615565077185550" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br /><br />For mysteries by this same author, see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8307827.John_A__Flanagan" title="John A. Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">John A. Flanagan</a>.<br /><br />John Flanagan grew up in Sydney, Australia, hoping to be a writer. It wasn't until he wrote a highly uncomplimentary poem about a senior executive at the agency where he worked, however, that his talent was revealed. It turned out one of the company directors agreed with John's assessment of the executive, and happily agreed to train John in copywriting. <br /><br />After writing advertising copy for the next two decades, John teamed with an old friend to develop a television sitcom, Hey Dad!, which went on to air for eight years. <br /><br />John began writing Ranger's Apprentice for his son, Michael, ten years ago, and is still hard at work on the series. <br /><br />He currently lives in a suburb of Manly, Australia, with his wife. In addition to their son, they have two grown daughters and four grandsons.</span>
